  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('rating_details').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

Aber in Wirklichkeit betrügen sie die Menschen um diese ersparte Zeit. Als die Not am größten ist und die Welt ihnen schon endgültig zu gehören scheint, entschließt sich Meister Hora, der geheimnisvolle "Verwalter der Zeit", zum Eingreifen. Doch dazu braucht er d</span>
  <span id="freeText8862786380109232418" style="display:none">Eine gespenstische Gesellschaft "grauer Herren" ist am Werk und veranlasst immer mehr Menschen, Zeit zu sparen. Aber in Wirklichkeit betrügen sie die Menschen um diese ersparte Zeit. Als die Not am größten ist und die Welt ihnen schon endgültig zu gehören scheint, entschließt sich Meister Hora, der geheimnisvolle "Verwalter der Zeit", zum Eingreifen. Doch dazu braucht er die Hilfe eines Menschenkindes. Die Welt steht still und Momo, die struppige kleine Heldin der Geschichte, kämpft ganz allein, mit nichts als einer Blume in der Hand und einer Schildkröte unter dem Arm, gegen das riesige Heer der "grauen Herren".</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">If you have just started studying German it won't be the easiest read, no book is when you're only beginning another language, but once you're interme<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">If you have just started studying German it won't be the easiest read, no book is when you're only beginning another language, but once you're intermediate by all means read it because it's one of the most magical and beautiful books you'll ever read! You'll have to look up words from time to time but I promise it will be worth the effort because it will teach you the words that add colour, texture and magic and really gives a language wings.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

It's a children's book (suitable for kids 10 years and older in my estimation), but it's compelling, thrilling, and wonderf<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Depends on what she likes.       $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_943').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer1425859934667966311">Manny was working late one evening when he received an unexpected visitor. He was an old man with white hair and gold-rimmed glasses, curiously dressed in a lace-embroidered doublet and a periwig, and he was carrying a book.<br/><br/>"Greetings," said the visitor. "I think you should read this."<br/><br/>"What is it?" asked Manny irritably. People were always asking him to read things. "I don't really have time right now.   <span id="freeText1425859934667966311" style="display:none">Manny was working late one evening when he received an unexpected visitor. He was an old man with white hair and gold-rimmed glasses, curiously dressed in a lace-embroidered doublet and a periwig, and he was carrying a book.<br /><br />"Greetings," said the visitor. "I think you should read this."<br /><br />"What is it?" asked Manny irritably. People were always asking him to read things. "I don't really have time right now. I need to get this software problem fixed for tomorrow. And then I have an article to write and a dozen emails to answer and some insurance paperwork I've been putting off for too long. I'm very busy. How did you get in, anyway?"<br /><br />"It <i>definitely</i> sounds like you should read <i>Momo</i>," said the old man, ignoring Manny's question. "I am quite concerned about you. Here, take a look."<br /><br />Manny flicked through it briefly and sighed. "It's some kind of YA fantasy novel, right?" he said. <br /><br />"If that is what you want to call it," replied the visitor.<br /><br />"But I don't read YA," said Manny. "All my friends know that."<br /><br />"Why not?" asked the visitor.<br /><br />"Well, I'm too old for it," said Manny, as he studied the error message his laptop was showing him. "I find it painfully unsophisticated and badly written. It never gives me anything."<br /><br />"Perhaps you should become younger," said the visitor. "It's quite easy, you know."<br /><br />"Really?" said Manny in a dismissive tone. But something made him glance up from his screen, and he saw to his surprise that the visitor was no longer an old man. In fact, he almost looked like a child.<br /><br />"You see?" said the visitor. "Now, here's what you need to do. Just learn German. At first, you'll be a helpless infant and you won't be able to read at all. Soon, though, you'll find you're four or five and enjoying stories. When you're about ten, you'll be ready for this. I'll come back when you've finished."<br /><br />"You must be joking," said Manny, who was looking at his screen again. "Didn't I just tell you I was very busy?" He turned around, but found his visitor had disappeared. All that was left was a large pile of German children's books.<br /><br />Over the next few months, Manny somehow found himself reading one German book after another. He read <i>Grimms Märchen</i>, and <i>Krabat</i>, and <i>Das doppelte Lottchen</i>, and <i>Madita</i>, and <i>Karlsson vom Dach</i>. Finally, a couple of weeks before Christmas, he opened <i>Momo</i>. He found he couldn't put it down. He had just finished the last chapter when he heard someone clear their throat behind him. <br /><br />"Well?" said the visitor. "I hope you're not too busy to talk to me?"<br /><br />"Uh, no," said Manny. "It's funny, but when I think about it I find I have more time than I'd imagined. And you're right. <i>Momo</i> is very good."<br /><br />"I'm glad to hear it," said the visitor gravely.<br /><br />"There was just something I wanted to ask you," said Manny. "Here, wait a moment." He leafed through the book to find the page. But when he looked up, the visitor had gone again.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1425859934667966311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_660914752" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/660914752" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/660914752?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783522119405" href="/book/show/68813.Momo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=german">german</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer660914752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2338678816720246659">Momo = The Grey Gentlemen = The Men in Grey, Michael Ende<br/><br/><b>Momo</b>, also known as <b>The Grey Gentlemen</b> or <b>The Men in Grey</b>, is a fantasy novel by <b>Michael Ende</b>, published in 1973. <br/><br/>It is about the concept of time and how it is used by humans in modern societies. In the ruins of an amphitheater just outside an unnamed city lives Momo, a little girl of mysterious origin. She came to the ruin, parent-less and wearing a long, used coat. She is illiterate and cannot count, and she doesn't know how old she is. </span>
  <span id="freeText2338678816720246659" style="display:none">Momo = The Grey Gentlemen = The Men in Grey, Michael Ende<br /><br /><b>Momo</b>, also known as <b>The Grey Gentlemen</b> or <b>The Men in Grey</b>, is a fantasy novel by <b>Michael Ende</b>, published in 1973. <br /><br />It is about the concept of time and how it is used by humans in modern societies. In the ruins of an amphitheater just outside an unnamed city lives Momo, a little girl of mysterious origin. She came to the ruin, parent-less and wearing a long, used coat. She is illiterate and cannot count, and she doesn't know how old she is. When asked, she replies, <i>"As far as I remember, I've always been around."</i> <br /><br />She is remarkable in the neighborhood because she has the extraordinary ability to listen—really listen. By simply being with people and listening to them, she can help them find answers to their problems, make up with each other, and think of fun games. The advice given to people <i>"go and see Momo!"</i> has become a household phrase and Momo makes many friends, especially an honest, silent street-cleaner, Beppo, and a poetic, extroverted tour guide, Gigi (Guido in some translations). This pleasant atmosphere is spoiled by the arrival of the Men in Grey, eventually revealed as a species of paranormal parasites stealing the time of humans. <br /><br />Appearing in the form of grey-clad, grey-skinned, bald men, these strange individuals present themselves as representing the timesavings Bank and promote the idea of "timesaving" among the population: supposedly, time can be deposited in the Bank and returned to the client later with interest. After encountering the Men in Grey, people are made to forget all about them, but not about the resolution to save as much time as possible for later use. <br /><br />Gradually, the sinister influence of the Men in Grey affects the whole city: life becomes sterile, devoid of all things considered time-wasting, like social activities, recreation, art, imagination, or sleeping. Buildings and clothing are made exactly the same for everyone, and the rhythms of life become hectic. In reality, the more time people save, the less they have; the time they save is actually lost to them. Instead, it is consumed by the Men in Grey in the form of cigars made from the dried petals of the hour-lilies that represent time. Without these cigars the Men in Grey cannot exist.<br /><br />Momo, however, is a wrench in the plans of the Men in Grey and the Timesavings Bank, thanks to her special personality. The Men in Grey try various plans to deal with her, to derail her from stopping their scheme, but they all fail. <br /><br />When even her closest friends fall under the influence of the Men in Grey in one way or another, Momo's only hope to save the time of mankind are the administrator of Time, Master Secundus Minutus Hora, and Cassiopeia, a tortoise who can communicate through writing on her shell and can see thirty minutes into the future. <br /><br />Momo's adventure takes her from the depths of her heart, which her own time flows from in the form of lovely hour-lilies, to the lair of the Men in Grey themselves, where the time that people believe they are saving is hoarded. After Master Hora stops time, but gives Momo one hour-lily to carry with her, she has exactly one hour to defeat the Men in Grey in a frozen world where only they and she are still moving. <br /><br />She surreptitiously follows them to their underground lair and observes as they decimate their own number in order to stretch their supply of time as far as possible. With the advice of Cassiopeia and by using the hour-lily, Momo is able to shut the door to their vault. Facing extinction as soon as their cigars are consumed, the few remaining Men in Grey pursue Momo, perishing one by one. The very last Man in Grey finally begs her to give him the hour-lily, and when she refuses, he too vanishes remarking that "it is good it is over".<br /><br />Using the very last minute she has before her hour-lily crumbles, Momo opens the vault again, releasing the millions of hour-lilies stored within. The stolen time returns to its proper owners and goes back to their hearts, causing time to start again (without people knowing it had ever halted). Momo is reunited with her friends, and elsewhere Master Hora rejoices together with Cassiopeia.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش:روز سوم ماه آگوست سال 1984 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: مومو؛ نویسنده: میشائیل انده؛ مترجم: محمد زرین بال؛ تهران، ابتکار، 1363؛ در 317ص؛ چاپ دیگر: ابتکار نو، در 1386؛ 325ص؛ شابک ایکس - 964657940؛ چاپ سوم در 300ص؛ 1393؛ شابک 9789646579408؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان آلمانی - سده 20م<br /><br />ظاهرا کتاب کودک و نوجوان است، ولی انگار چنان نیست؛ موجودات خاکستری پوش، وقت و گذر زمان مردمان را میدزدند، و مردمان به تدریج، برای همصحبتی با «دوستان»، «آب دادن به گلها»، و «گام زدن در خیابان»، دیگر وقت ندارند،...؛ در حین خواندن کتاب شاید شمایان هم فکر کنید که مومو هستید، یا اینکه باید باشید! آنوقت برای شنیدن حرفهای دیگران، و برای خودتان هم، همیشه وقت خواهید داشت؛ بویژه برای گلدانها و بچه ها؛ همیشه از اینکه دیگران اینهمه سرشان شلوغ است، تعجب خواهید کرد، برای به رویا رفتن، هم خیلی وقت خواهید داشت؛ خیلی...؛ خاکستری پوشها هر چندتا، که از دوستان شما را گرفته باشند، اما هنوز باز هم خیلیها هستند، که برای شنیدن حرفهای آنها پیش شما خواهند آمد؛ «مومو»، رمانی آلمانی ست، که در سال 1972میلادی توسط «میشائل انده»، پا به جهان ادبیات گذاشت، و در جای جای دنیا، به اسامی گوناگو،ن همچون «مردان خاکستری»، و یا «مردان خاکستری پوش»، ترجمه شد؛ عنوان اصلی کتاب، به زبان آلمانی «مو مو» و یا «داستان عجیب زمان ربایان، و کودکی که زمان ربوده شده را، به مردم بازگرداند» است، کتاب در سال 1973میلادی، برنده ی یکی از جوایز ادبی آلمان شد؛ داستان درباره ی زمان، و طرز استفاده از آن در جوامع مدرن بشری ست؛ «میشائل انده»، برای خلق رمان، همچون رمان معروف دیگرش «داستان بی پایان»، از فانتزی و نمادگرایی، برای رویارویی با طبیعت و نشان دادن اهمیت زمان، توانمندی قصه ها، دوستی، همدردی و چیزهای کوچکی که چاشنی زندگی هستند، همیشه بهره برده است<br /><br />داستان «مومو» مشهورترین اثر «میشائل انده»، پس از «داستان بی پایان» است؛ خط اصلی داستان، درباره ی به چالش کشیدن مصرف گرایی، و کاستن از فشار روانی، ناشی از زندگی مدرن است؛ توضیحی است بر این، که چگونه سود و منفعت دسته ای خاص از جامعه، باعث تحمیل کردن شیوه ی ویژه ای از زندگی، بر دیگر مردمان میشود؛ در بسیاری از آثار «انده»، کودکانگی، نقش بسزایی بازی میکند؛ در «مومو»، کودک در برابر جامعه ی بزرگسال قرار میگیرد، و به این دلیل که کودکان، تمام زمان دنیا را، در اختیار دارند، هدف مردان خاکستری قرار میگیرند؛ اما کودکان قبول نمیکنند، که بازیهای کودکانه شان چیزی جز هدردادن وقت و زمان نیست؛ نویسنده با به سخره گرفتن «عروسک باربی»، و سایر اسباب بازیهای گران قیمت، برای بیان این که «چگونه هر کس حتی بصورت غیرمستقیم، میتواند قانع شود، که مصرف گرایی را برگزیند»، سود میبرد؛ «انده» میگوید که «مومو در ستایش از ایتالیا ست و همچنین بیانیه ای عاشقانه نیز هست»؛ کتاب پس از چاپ در آمریکا، مورد توجه منتقدان قرار نگرفت، و بهمین دلیل بیش از یکبار چاپ نشد؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4290275" />
    <a title="Kara Maia Spencer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/265011-kara-maia-spencer"><img alt="Kara Maia Spencer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216285781p2/265011.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4290275?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kara Maia Spencer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kara Maia Spencer" href="/user/show/265011-kara-maia-spencer">Kara Maia Spencer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA &amp; Adults</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4290275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12663938590174167658">Momo is a classic story that is known as a children's book, yet I believe that adults may even glean more from its reading than younger folk. Momo is written by Michael Ende, the author who is most known in the US for having written The Neverending Story. When I was younger, and my mother ran an independent children's bookstore, she ordered a case of this book, and gave a copy to all of her friends and colleagues.<br/><br/>This is a modern day fairytale, about a little girl named Momo, who moves into a ru</span>
  <span id="freeText12663938590174167658" style="display:none">Momo is a classic story that is known as a children's book, yet I believe that adults may even glean more from its reading than younger folk. Momo is written by Michael Ende, the author who is most known in the US for having written The Neverending Story. When I was younger, and my mother ran an independent children's bookstore, she ordered a case of this book, and gave a copy to all of her friends and colleagues.<br /><br />This is a modern day fairytale, about a little girl named Momo, who moves into a ruined amphitheater on the edge of a Italian-style town. She is a remarkable individual, who lives in poverty, yet her life is rich with friendship and love. Momo has a unique skill of deep listening. Soon all the villagers learn that when they are not getting along they should "go and see Momo". Through Momo's friendship, her friends find peace, community, and creativity. Her gift of listening to them until the truth unveils itself brings her to be surrounded by many friends who bring her food, tell her stories, and help care for her in her adopted home.<br /><br />Life changes quickly in the village, when the Men in Gray infiltrate their life, hypnotizing people to save time. In their Time Saving Banks, they steal people's time, and smoke it in gray cigars that they are never seen without. Yet, no one remembers ever seeing the Men in Gray, except Momo, who cannot be hypnotized by the lures of timesaving because she is content with being who she is and loves to spend time with her friends. Eventually, everyone is entrapped by the Men in Gray, and only Momo can save them.<br /><br />Even Momo's two best friends, Guido the Guide and Bebbo Roadsweeper, have been seduced by the Men in Gray. Luckily, she has help from two new friends Cassiopeia, a tortoise who can see precisely half-an-hour into the future and can spell words across her shell to communicate, and Professor Secundus Minutus Hora, who is the steward of the universal source of time.<br /><br />This is an incredibly magical story which I dare not tell you more of lest I ruin the story for you. You must read Momo for yourself. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12663938590174167658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_978102295" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/978102295" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480492067p2/32532774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/978102295?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=children">children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer978102295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9760058932753070581">Dear friends!<br/><br/>Do you have time to sit down for a moment, and listen to a story? It is a true one, of great importance, with a vital message for humankind. It starts in a classroom, where a teacher is about to wrap up for the day. She has put a lot of time into the Timesaving Bank, and wants to save some more of it by rushing off to the underground to catch the next train. That makes at least four minutes which she will not have to spend waiting, Heaven forbid! 4 minutes to put into the Timesaving</span>
  <span id="freeText9760058932753070581" style="display:none">Dear friends!<br /><br />Do you have time to sit down for a moment, and listen to a story? It is a true one, of great importance, with a vital message for humankind. It starts in a classroom, where a teacher is about to wrap up for the day. She has put a lot of time into the Timesaving Bank, and wants to save some more of it by rushing off to the underground to catch the next train. That makes at least four minutes which she will not have to spend waiting, Heaven forbid! 4 minutes to put into the Timesaving Bank.<br /><br />Just when she is about to rush out, already wearing her coat, some of her mentor students come in. There has been a conflict. They want to tell her their different versions. The teacher sighs, sacrifices her valuable time out of a reluctant sense of duty, and lets go of the next underground, quite unwillingly. <br /><br />What follows is a 40-minute conversation between five teenage boys, all describing the development of the fight from their point of view. <br /><br />Having been assigned to do unspecified online research in a class, they find themselves bored, and start to tease each other. After a while, it is not funny anymore, someone gets hurt, tries to pay back with a spiteful comment, and the whole thing gets out of control. This is not what the teacher hears first, of course. The last comment in class is the first that is reported: "He said...", "But you did...", uncovering of the drama in backwards slow motion.<br /><br />After 40 minutes of intensive listening and peeling the onion, a solution is found, apologies are accepted, and all leave to go home. One student gets into new trouble with his timesaving mother who had to wait for him and lost an entire 60 minute investment in the Timesaving Bank. Peacekeeping is expensive!<br /><br />Change of scenes. The teacher enters her own home, late. Her children hang out in the living room, reading. In order to vent the stress caused by the lost time, the teacher, now transformed into a mother, retells the whole story again, with all the strange tosses and turns before the truth is revealed.<br /><br />Her eldest son looks up, smiles, and says:<br /><br />"Why don't you ask Momo, mum?"<br /><br />That question has a familiar ring to it. It is a quote from a long-ago favourite. The mother, confused, looks at the title of the book the son is reading, and sees the cover of Michael Ende's perfect fairytale. The 14-year-old is rereading the story that he had loved to listen to as a small child, a story of such power that it gains strength every time you enter it.<br /><br />A story of a child who teaches grown-ups a lesson.<br /><br />"Why don't you ask Momo, mum?" My son is teaching me a lesson.<br /><br />In an amphitheatre outside a big city, the girl Momo lives and assembles her friends. She has a rare gift: she can listen! This gift helps people talk and solve problems, come to terms with misunderstandings and find back to a friendly way with each others. The city, however, is in danger. Grey men have taken over, encouraging people to "save time". They put new structures in place to make things faster, and more efficient. But at the same time, something is lost: the appreciation of life lived for the moment. Education is turned into mindless infotainment with standardised rules:<br /><br />"All the games were selected for them by supervisors and had to have some useful, educational purpose. The children learned these new games but unlearned something else in the process: they forgot to be happy, how to take pleasure in little things and last, but not least, how to dream."<br /><br />In the grown-up world, hate and mistrust enter the stage:<br /><br />"All the world's misfortunes stemmed from the countless untruths, both deliberate and unintentional, which people told because of haste or carelessness."<br /><br />What is to be done? The little girl Momo sets out to save the world by reconquering time!<br /><br />If you think this sounds like a boring, philosophical read for children, think again. It is one of the most compellingly exciting stories imaginable, capturing a teenage boy (who already knew the plot) so completely that he forgot time and place to finish it in one session yesterday. It is so touching that he came down to breakfast today and said that he had actually cried, adding:<br /><br />"And that has not happened in many years, mum, not since I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/161099.Good_Night__Mr__Tom" title="Good Night, Mr. Tom by Michelle Magorian" rel="nofollow noopener">Good Night, Mr. Tom</a>. Maybe you should read it with your class?"<br /><br />"I don't have time for that!"<br /><br />"Mum!"<br /><br />"We don't have a copy in English!"<br /><br />"Yes, we do. In the school library. You bought it yourself!"<br /><br />"Did I?"<br /><br />So my students will not do standardised peer collaboration games for mentor time from now on. They will sit in a circle, pretending it is an amphitheatre, and they will listen to their teacher read "Momo":<br /><br />"Time is life itself, and life resides in the human heart."<br /><br />And since we have plenty of time, we will continue with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27712.The_Neverending_Story" title="The Neverending Story by Michael Ende" rel="nofollow noopener">The Neverending Story</a>, another masterpiece by the same author. It will take a while, but I can't think of time better invested. What a waste of life to save time!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9760058932753070581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/570544487?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2019-shelf">2019-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570544487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16859523389771011087">What was I thinking? I already count Ende's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27712.The_Neverending_Story' title='The Neverending Story by Michael Ende' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Neverending Story</a> to be one of the very best books ever written, so why would I waste SO MUCH TIME getting to anything else he wrote?<br/><br/>It blows my mind!<br/><br/>It's almost like SOMEONE HAS BEEN STEALING MY TIME! All those damn time-savers out there fooled me and tied me up and made my life a dull gray, smoke-filled, DEADLY TEDIOUS world! They kept me from this book... and now I know why!<br/><br/>It's a conspiracy of the Time-Banks.<br/><br/>Momo is pretty damn wonderful. The c</span>
  <span id="freeText16859523389771011087" style="display:none">What was I thinking? I already count Ende's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27712.The_Neverending_Story" title="The Neverending Story by Michael Ende" rel="nofollow noopener">The Neverending Story</a> to be one of the very best books ever written, so why would I waste SO MUCH TIME getting to anything else he wrote?<br /><br />It blows my mind!<br /><br />It's almost like SOMEONE HAS BEEN STEALING MY TIME! All those damn time-savers out there fooled me and tied me up and made my life a dull gray, smoke-filled, DEADLY TEDIOUS world! They kept me from this book... and now I know why!<br /><br />It's a conspiracy of the Time-Banks.<br /><br />Momo is pretty damn wonderful. The concept is classic, an epic battle between children who really understand the necessity of wasting time and the horrible monsters, the gray men, who offer up devilish riches to everyone else in order to suck the life and time from everyone else.<br /><br />*shiver*<br /><br />Honestly, if someone published this as the new up-and-coming YA book in today's day and age without knowing that Momo ever existed, it would be heralded as unique and gorgeous and groundbreaking. Gaiman would be blurbing it and there would be a twitter storm of praise.<br /><br />But no, it's just some silly book written back in 1973. No one cares. ; ;<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16859523389771011087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7773243080199623157">This turned out to be a charming book and one I had never heard of before, although I very much enjoyed one of Ende's other works <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27712.The_Neverending_Story' title='The Neverending Story by Michael Ende' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Neverending Story</a> many years ago.<br/><br/>Although <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45858708.Momo' title='Momo by Michael Ende' rel='nofollow noopener'>Momo</a> was first published in 1973 the story it tells applies perfectly to today.   <span id="freeText7773243080199623157" style="display:none">This turned out to be a charming book and one I had never heard of before, although I very much enjoyed one of Ende's other works <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27712.The_Neverending_Story" title="The Neverending Story by Michael Ende" rel="nofollow noopener">The Neverending Story</a> many years ago.<br /><br />Although <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45858708.Momo" title="Momo by Michael Ende" rel="nofollow noopener">Momo</a> was first published in 1973 the story it tells applies perfectly to today. A city is besieged by sinister grey men whose job it is to steal time, leaving the inhabitants believing they have no time left for 'unnecessary' things like enjoyment or caring for others, even their own children. Momo is the only person who is able to fight back against the grey men but even she needs help from Professor Hora who lives outside time.<br /><br />This is a beautifully written fantasy about a young girl who saves the world but there is a strong moral there as well. The people who try to save time end up being sad and stressed with no light in their lives. Their children have huge, expensive toys which need no imagination to play with. It all suddenly sounds a bit real.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45858708.Momo" title="Momo by Michael Ende" rel="nofollow noopener">Momo</a> is a children's book which is also a perfect read for grown ups. I enjoyed it very much.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer263908105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15059591705189156858">I read this book for the first time as a preteen, but I left it unfinished because I didn't find it engaging or entertaining. A few years later, due to my LOVE for Michaels Endes's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/366650293' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Neverending Story</a>, I decided to give it another try, and managed to finish it that time.<br/>In the end, I quite liked the story, I found it very beautiful actually. My problem with it is that it isn't a diverting read, I found it boring in many occasions, which it is a shame because <b>the message that this story sends i</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15059591705189156858" style="display:none">I read this book for the first time as a preteen, but I left it unfinished because I didn't find it engaging or entertaining. A few years later, due to my LOVE for Michaels Endes's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/366650293" rel="nofollow noopener">The Neverending Story</a>, I decided to give it another try, and managed to finish it that time.<br />In the end, I quite liked the story, I found it very beautiful actually. My problem with it is that it isn't a diverting read, I found it boring in many occasions, which it is a shame because <b>the message that this story sends is very beautiful</b>. I don't think this book has the right pace for a story intended for kids or young people, it is a miss in this area. The essence is definitely there, <b>it is meaningful</b>, but the first time I tried to read it I was too young to have the patience to see it through, and I think many young people must have found themselves in the same situation. Again, it is a pity because it could have been more transcendental with just a little more agility in its rhythm.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15059591705189156858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_806955" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/806955" />
    <a title="Dane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3554-dane"><img alt="Dane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1171369071p2/3554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/806955?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dane" href="/user/show/3554-dane">Dane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/27718.Momo">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of lighthearted literature</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3554-dane?shelf=fiction-read">fiction-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer806955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1340175457118467784">You cannot, repeat: cannot, go into this book with the expectations of "hard," realist fiction. Then again, if you know anything about Michael Ende (the author of the Never Ending Story), you won't.<br/><br/>Momo is one of those rare books that would do well in a fourth-grade classes, but is also strangely releveant to adults. The story centers around a girl named Momo who took residence in an ancient, abandoned amphitheater in an unnamed town, which is populated by a series of people who do small-town jo</span>
  <span id="freeText1340175457118467784" style="display:none">You cannot, repeat: cannot, go into this book with the expectations of "hard," realist fiction. Then again, if you know anything about Michael Ende (the author of the Never Ending Story), you won't.<br /><br />Momo is one of those rare books that would do well in a fourth-grade classes, but is also strangely releveant to adults. The story centers around a girl named Momo who took residence in an ancient, abandoned amphitheater in an unnamed town, which is populated by a series of people who do small-town jobs (Bepo Streetsweeper, Nino who owns an inn, Guido Guide who works as a fake - albeit enterataining - tourist guide). <br /><br />The story starts by painting Momo's life and place in the town, and details the downfall of the place to mysterious, grey men. The book deals heavily in the subject of time, and the squandering of it - and this is the genius of the plot. There is enough fantasy to hold a 10-year-old's attention, but plenty of substance to whet the apetite of an adult.<br /><br />I can't help but think that this story rings of pre-globalized Europe, and considering that Ende is German, that would make sense. Momo is translated from German, and the diction often shows this, but that doesn't stop the book from being an incredibly enjoyable read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1340175457118467784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/579547053?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Smartarse" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse">Ms. Smartarse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=german">german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer579547053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7909851503173646266"><em>Translated into English, under the same title: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27718.Momo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Momo</a>.</em><br/><br/>At the edge of a small town, among the ruins of an old amphitheater, lives a most unusual little girl. She is very small, very poor and not particularly educated for her age. She does, however, have an <em>extraordinary</em> talent: she can truly <em>listen</em> to people.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436213015i/15432912._SX540_.jpg' width='400' alt='Momo listens' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Don't mistake her listening skills for the generic <em>I will listen for now, but please hurry up so I can talk about my own problems</em> type. Hers is the genuine kind, the one that shows real interes</span>
  <span id="freeText7909851503173646266" style="display:none"><em>Translated into English, under the same title: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27718.Momo" rel="nofollow noopener">Momo</a>.</em><br><br>At the edge of a small town, among the ruins of an old amphitheater, lives a most unusual little girl. She is very small, very poor and not particularly educated for her age. She does, however, have an <em>extraordinary</em> talent: she can truly <em>listen</em> to people.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436213015i/15432912._SX540_.jpg" width="400" alt="Momo listens" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Don't mistake her listening skills for the generic <em>I will listen for now, but please hurry up so I can talk about my own problems</em> type. Hers is the genuine kind, the one that shows real interest in people's problems. This amazing ability of hers has proven to be so successful, that eventually "just go and talk to Momo about it" had rightfully become the solution to anyone's problems.<br><br>The town's happy life is suddenly cut short when the <em>grey men</em> start showing up. Before long, people are putting their "extra" time into their bank, getting busier and unhappier every day. Only Momo seems to have escaped the grey men's influence...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436212980i/15432891._SX540_.jpg" alt="Children playing" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really wish I had read this story when I was a child, instead of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27712.The_Neverending_Story" title="The Neverending Story by Michael Ende" rel="nofollow noopener">The Neverending Story</a>. It's so much more engaging, realistic and - to a certain extent - rather sad. Alas, at the time, there was this big hype about a movie, so I ended up reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15619.Michael_Ende" title="Michael Ende" rel="nofollow noopener"> Michael Ende</a>'s other book. ... and that <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=geVYIHOat5o" rel="nofollow noopener">theme song</a> still gets occasionally stuck in my head.<br><br>Strictly as a children's story, it's one of the better ones I've read. However when it comes to those children's stories which I've read as an adult, it is somewhat lacking. <br>Most characters can be reduced to a single attribute, the only exception being of the Time Guardian. Even <em>he</em> was basically just <em>slightly</em> more real (in behavior) compared to the rest of the cast.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436213513i/15432944._SX540_.jpg" width="400" alt="It's raining flower petals" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>Score : 3.3/5 stars</strong><br><br>The world -building of the story, however is awesome. The little allegories here and there paint an amazing picture, especially now, that I am looking at them with the eyes of an adult (*cough* wishfulthinking *cough*).<br>A definite must-read, when it comes to children's literature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7909851503173646266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_113855150" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <a title="Dan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan" href="/user/show/1200006-dan">Dan</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer113855150" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer405773020551667296">I bought this book several months ago at a used book store, but I put off reading it because I was afraid it wouldn't live up to Michael Ende's other famous book, which also happens to be my favorite book, The Neverending Story. While Momo isn't as complex and more bluntly allegorical, it is charming and emotionally stunning. Perhaps I am more naive than most readers, but I felt myself swept up into this book's persuasive world in which children are forgetting how to play and adults only care ab</span>
  <span id="freeText405773020551667296" style="display:none">I bought this book several months ago at a used book store, but I put off reading it because I was afraid it wouldn't live up to Michael Ende's other famous book, which also happens to be my favorite book, The Neverending Story. While Momo isn't as complex and more bluntly allegorical, it is charming and emotionally stunning. Perhaps I am more naive than most readers, but I felt myself swept up into this book's persuasive world in which children are forgetting how to play and adults only care about saving time instead of enjoying life--a world, of course, very much like our own.<br /><br />I was at times amused, delighted, and deeply moved by this little book. There aren't many books I've read in a day, but I was literally reading this as I walked around the city because I simply couldn't stop reading. There are some books which genuinely affected the way I see the world, and I have a strong belief this one has become one of those.<br /><br />Though more jaded and literary readers might balk at this book's childlike naivite, I believe anyone who gives this book a chance will fall under its spell.</span>
  <a data-text-id="405773020551667296" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2649471819" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2649471819" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45400990-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573825853p2/45400990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2649471819?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/45400990-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/17155494-momo">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2649471819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14726341615197033780"><b>
  <i>Anni's pick for my "Tell me your favorite standalone and I'll read it" BINGO</i>
</b><br/><br/>I didn't even know this book existed till Anni recommended it. And boy am I glad I read it! Because it was so lovely and charming!!! Fabulous!<br/><br/>Momo, is a ragged little waif, who had set up house beneath the stage of an old ruined amphitheatre. Small and thin, with an unruly mop of jet-black hair that looked as if it had never seen a comb or a pair of scissors, she is most always barefoot and wears an ankle-length dres</span>
  <span id="freeText14726341615197033780" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Anni's pick for my "Tell me your favorite standalone and I'll read it" BINGO</i>
</b><br><br>I didn't even know this book existed till Anni recommended it. And boy am I glad I read it! Because it was so lovely and charming!!! Fabulous!<br><br>Momo, is a ragged little waif, who had set up house beneath the stage of an old ruined amphitheatre. Small and thin, with an unruly mop of jet-black hair that looked as if it had never seen a comb or a pair of scissors, she is most always barefoot and wears an ankle-length dress that's more like a mass of patches of different colours and over it, a too big for her man's jacket with the sleeves turned up at the wrists. In a word, she is <b>different!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1553332025i/27254050.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Momo - the movie</i><br><br>But despite being different, or perhaps precisely because of it, Momo becomes indispensable to the people in the neighbourhood. She couldn't sing like a bird or play an instrument, she couldn't do tricks and knew no magic either. <br><b>'No. What Momo was better at than anyone else was <i>listening.</i><br>Anyone can listen, you may say - what's so special about that? - but you'd be wrong. Very few people know how to listen properly and Momo's way of listening was quite unique.'</b><br><br>I'm not going to spoil and tell you how unique, you'll have to read and find that out. Suffice it to say that her way of listening made the words <i>"Why not go and see Momo?" a stock phrase with the local inhabitants.</i><br><br>One day, sinister men in grey arrive and are silently starting to take over the city. They are drawing life-blood from the unsuspecting inhabitants. They are the time-thieves. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1553334759i/27254187._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>The men in grey - Momo the movie</i><br><br><b>
  <i>Lots of things take time and time was Momo's only form of wealth.</i>
</b><br>So of course she is the first to notice that something is wrong. <br><br>Everyone started to "save" time for later. They started to rush and to hurry, to fall prey to the men in grey.<br>And<br><b>
  <i>People never seemed to notice that by saving time they were loosing something else. No one cared to admit that life was becoming even poorer, bleaker and more monotonous. The ones who felt this most keenly were the children, because no one had time for them anymore. But time is life itself and life resides in the human heart. And the more people saved the less they had.</i>
</b> <br><br>Momo, with her uncanny ability to listen, her simplicity and honesty, holds the key to salvation. She is the only one who can resist these soulless, corrupt creatures. So she sets out to destroy them and wrestle the time of her friends back from them.<br>Guided by a strangely gifted tortoise, Cassiopeia, Momo finds her way to the mysterious Professor Hora, who promises help her.<br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1553338391i/27254309._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Cassiopeia with words appearing on her shell: "KOMM MIT - German for FOLLOW ME -Momo the movie</i><br><br>I will not tell you what adventures Momo and Cassiopeia go through. You'll have to read to find that out. I'll only say that their journey was wonderful and exciting!<br><br>Peppered with passages that make the reader stop and think about time and life, and the meaning of living, this compelling story is one for readers of all ages. Intricate and deep, it challenges us to take a step back and reflect. Because after all,<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1553338391i/27254310._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><i>Momo - Michael Ende quote</i><br><br>and it's like this:<br><b>
  <i>'Sometimes, when you've a very long street ahead of you, you think how terribly long it is and feel sure you'll never get it swept. .. And then you start to hurry... You work fater and faster and every time you look up there seems to be just as much left to sweep as before and you try even harder, and you panic, and in the end you're out of breath and have to stop - and still the street stretches away in front of you. That's not the way to do it.<br>You must never think of the whole street at once, understand? You must only concentrate on the next step, the next breath, the next stroke of the broom, and the next, and the next. Nothing else.'</i>
</b><br><br>In a grown-up world of hate, mistrust and haste in the pursuit of material gain,<br><b>
  <i>"All the world's misfortunes stemmed from the countless untruths, both deliberate and unintentional, which people told because of haste or carelessness."</i>
</b><br><br>This is the story of a child teaching the grown-ups a lesson. The lesson that: <b>
  <i>"Time is life itself, and life resides in the human heart."</i>
</b><br><br>And since we have plenty of time, we should make sure we listen!<br>Happy reading! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14726341615197033780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2649471819">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2215310787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16716605641981613393">A wonderful book for children (and those who have left childhood behind but are looking for a ray of hope to keep them sane). Momo is a little girl about to be swallowed by a world where men dressed in gray are working hard to steal people's time. No one has time for stories now, or games, but Momo won't let these men and this new world take away her friends, she will fight for them and save them from a destiny of regrets.<br/>Beautifully written and full of heart.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_170263234" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170263234" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4269230-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300191814p2/4269230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170263234?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/4269230-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/17155494-momo">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4269230-michelle?shelf=enriching-symbolism">enriching-symbolism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4269230-michelle?shelf=weird-is-cool">weird-is-cool</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4269230-michelle?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4269230-michelle?shelf=and-smart-too">and-smart-too</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4269230-michelle?shelf=couldn-t-put-it-down">couldn-t-put-it-down</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170263234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10782016782891056946">THIS is how to write a novel-length fairy tale. The characters are whole and human, the fantasy pure, and all else perfect. I must have more of Michael Ende's work.<br/> Some stories that deal with magic don't explain anything, not even the rules by which their magic operates. Others make too many rules, turning it into a confusing science. Not so here. Like fairy tales, we are introduced to a magical object, told the rules which constrain it, but now HOW it works, and move on. The reader is not left</span>
  <span id="freeText10782016782891056946" style="display:none">THIS is how to write a novel-length fairy tale. The characters are whole and human, the fantasy pure, and all else perfect. I must have more of Michael Ende's work.<br /> Some stories that deal with magic don't explain anything, not even the rules by which their magic operates. Others make too many rules, turning it into a confusing science. Not so here. Like fairy tales, we are introduced to a magical object, told the rules which constrain it, but now HOW it works, and move on. The reader is not left in the dust, but the mystery and wonder are whole.<br /> Symbolism in fairy tales is often very obvious, but the very structure of the genre permits this. I'm not talking about the idiotic good people=beautiful and evil people=ugly that none of the characters--except maybe the Author's Pet--can see through, but how good and evil take off their masks in Fantasy Land. Good can be a withered old man or a ragged and dirty child as well as a fairy princess, and evil is just as recognizable in a bowler hat as in a horned helmet. And yet, everyone has a personality, and even the villains are treated as people by the author.<br /> Fairy tales are more true than reality. This is how to convey a clear message that actually enhances the story. The men in grey may not be real, but we all know time-savers, Beppos and Guidos. If we're lucky, we may even know a Momo. In some urban fantasies, authors will sometimes mock popular culture, despite it not adding anything to the story. Modern toys that do everything for the child, leaving nothing to the imagination, are stripped of their glamor and shown for what they are, adding to the depth of the book instead of allowing the author to snicker at how unbelievably STUPID so-and-so is.<br /> If you intend to write fantasy, read this book. If you just enjoy reading fantasy, read this book. If you like a good story, read this book. If people tell you to read more, start here. It is brilliant, but not difficult, and the more you read it, the more you will gain.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10782016782891056946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2841184519" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2841184519" />
    <a title="Denisa Arsene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43388480-denisa-arsene"><img alt="Denisa Arsene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580911704p2/43388480.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2841184519?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denisa Arsene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denisa Arsene" href="/user/show/43388480-denisa-arsene">Denisa Arsene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43388480-denisa-arsene?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2841184519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6096869112805871178">Momo's parable is a story that, unfortunately, nowadays, more and more people live. we are trying to save as much time as we can by meeting goals that we alone or others impose on us. We only have a quick transition through life (in general) without having much time to sit with ourselves, to listen to us and to others, to nature, to life. We eat fast, we read fast, we go fast, we work fast, we want everything to go in a hurry to get ... where? It's an idea that has been grinding me for years. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText6096869112805871178" style="display:none">Momo's parable is a story that, unfortunately, nowadays, more and more people live. we are trying to save as much time as we can by meeting goals that we alone or others impose on us. We only have a quick transition through life (in general) without having much time to sit with ourselves, to listen to us and to others, to nature, to life. We eat fast, we read fast, we go fast, we work fast, we want everything to go in a hurry to get ... where? It's an idea that has been grinding me for years. The end is only one and I look, horrified, as more people run to him. For beyond all we expect only death. And yet, Momo teaches us that we are already living dead. We exist. Simple. We do not live. Consumer society is spreading more and more - if it does not already exist all over the world. And what do we consume? Goods? Not. We consume ourselves. Our life. This is the last idea of ​​the book, as I understand it and how it grinds me personally for years. I think it's time to wake up a little. Let's give us time. To know each other. To get along. Let's rest. Let's really live. Let's move slowly, conscious on the road of life and marvel and enrich us with every step and every experience.<br />I do love parables! </span>
  <a data-text-id="6096869112805871178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15800024372292846084">I had the pleasure of getting this book read to me by my 12 year old son as part of his schoolwork. Since I managed to never read it myself when I was a child (I was one of those types who never touched anything that was recommended to me by adults ^^'), I was glad to see that his teacher had picked it up for class.<br/><br/>Michael Ende's imagination is wonderful and the topic of this nearly 50 year old book is as vital today as it was back then - or better, even more important in our time of virtual gam</span>
  <span id="freeText15800024372292846084" style="display:none">I had the pleasure of getting this book read to me by my 12 year old son as part of his schoolwork. Since I managed to never read it myself when I was a child (I was one of those types who never touched anything that was recommended to me by adults ^^'), I was glad to see that his teacher had picked it up for class.<br /><br />Michael Ende's imagination is wonderful and the topic of this nearly 50 year old book is as vital today as it was back then - or better, even more important in our time of virtual gaming and sitting in front of one screen or the other the whole day.<br /><br />In the person of the loveable homeless girl Momo Ende opens the eyes of the people to those things that are really important in life, as she fights out her lonely battle against the Grey Gentlemen and their attempt to turn everybody into soulless, joyless yet effective citizens. (I would love to know if Terry Pratchett did read this, because my son and I were so reminded of the Auditors from the Discworld).<br /><br />Momo is a beautiful timeless story about … well … time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15800024372292846084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17992789358742640077" style="display:none">What is it about life that we truly treasure? <br />Let's take a minute and think.<br /><br />What did you think of?<br /><br />Imagine there comes a girl into your life, a small girl with brown eyes and brown unruly curls wearing a much too large men's jacket. Momo. This girl has the knack to listen and to play and to make everything in your life more beautiful.<br /><br />But one day the grey men come. They tell you that you're wasting your time with doing silly things like reading, telling stories, visiting your mum, writing poetry ... They tell you to save your time in their time bank.<br />You feel cold but persuaded and do as you're told.<br /><br />But the grey men are vampires stealing your time ... only Momo can see this.<br /><br />This is a beautiful tale about the importance of friendship, of the beauty of our lives and of infinite wisdom.<br />Many a saying in this book has impacted me deeply and I can only recommend it to young and old.</span>

<div id="review_1714637327" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1714637327?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanja Berg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanja Berg" href="/user/show/5935491-tanja-berg">Tanja Berg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783522201872" href="/book/show/18588669-momo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5935491-tanja-berg?shelf=german">german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5935491-tanja-berg?shelf=children-s-fantasy">children-s-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1714637327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3748659846967910928">This book has some truly stellar insights, but it does not make up for the fact that it is incredibly childish in places, and quite boring. I would have LOVED this when I was 10 years old. Now, not so much. <br/><br/>Momo, an orphan, makes a home for herslef in an abandoned amphitheater in some unnamed country; I immediately thought of Italy. She gets many friends of all ages because of her unusual abilitiy to listen. After a while Momo and her friends realize that things are changing in the city. It has </span>
  <span id="freeText3748659846967910928" style="display:none">This book has some truly stellar insights, but it does not make up for the fact that it is incredibly childish in places, and quite boring. I would have LOVED this when I was 10 years old. Now, not so much. <br /><br />Momo, an orphan, makes a home for herslef in an abandoned amphitheater in some unnamed country; I immediately thought of Italy. She gets many friends of all ages because of her unusual abilitiy to listen. After a while Momo and her friends realize that things are changing in the city. It has been invaded by grey men and no grown-ups have time for anything anymore. They are only interested in saving time, but for what, they don't have the time to say. Momo and her friends they must try to do something before it is too late.<br /><br />I read this in the original German, which was a lot easier than I had expected. Although the last book I read was something by Rebecca Gable and four times as long, with a grown-up audience, so I suppose I understimate my prowess. So I can't blame the translation, nor can I blame my lack of understanding the language. I got what Micahel Ende was saying, and some of it was very astute, I just didn't enjoy this very much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3748659846967910928" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

<span id="freeTextContainer5094882173769530665">This anniversary edition is beautiful, the illustrations quirky, the shape, size, cover of the book is lovely and I like the font. I simply dont like this translation anywhere <i>near</i> as much as the one by J.Maxwell Brownjohn. Lucas Zwirner's words somehow lose some of the magic of the first, simplified and less lyrical. It's still a gorgeous book, but I'm happier to read my little paperback for now. Maybe I'll add this to my bookshelf one day just for the sake of having it there.<br/><br/>It really makes yo</span>
  <span id="freeText5094882173769530665" style="display:none">This anniversary edition is beautiful, the illustrations quirky, the shape, size, cover of the book is lovely and I like the font. I simply dont like this translation anywhere <i>near</i> as much as the one by J.Maxwell Brownjohn. Lucas Zwirner's words somehow lose some of the magic of the first, simplified and less lyrical. It's still a gorgeous book, but I'm happier to read my little paperback for now. Maybe I'll add this to my bookshelf one day just for the sake of having it there.<br /><br />It really makes you appreciate the importance of a good translation, how the little nuances of text can completely change the feeling of a work. Now I <i>really<i></i> am hoping for a new translation of Cornelia Funke's Mirrorworld series - Anthea Bell's way with words is sorely lacking in that series, though the author's imagination is a gorgeous as ever.</i></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_78346534" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78346534" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/632452-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539718887p2/632452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78346534?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/632452-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78346534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10330313270588549909">I owe a debt of gratitude to a good friend for persuading me to read this novel. It is one that I would not have otherwise read, given the general premise and genre. A magical fable. I have one main point of information for you concerning this work that I will pass along right away so that you need not read the remainder of this review to have it. This is an extended fable of extraordinary charm that will captivate a reader of any age level. I can imagine an adult reading this book to a child an</span>
  <span id="freeText10330313270588549909" style="display:none">I owe a debt of gratitude to a good friend for persuading me to read this novel. It is one that I would not have otherwise read, given the general premise and genre. A magical fable. I have one main point of information for you concerning this work that I will pass along right away so that you need not read the remainder of this review to have it. This is an extended fable of extraordinary charm that will captivate a reader of any age level. I can imagine an adult reading this book to a child and both of them deriving so much from it simultaneously. It is a German <i>Wizard of Oz</i>.<br /><br />A bit past the halfway point of the novel, we encounter this riddle:<br /><br /><i>All dwelling in one house are strange brothers three,<br />as unlike as any three brothers could be,<br />yet try as you may to tell brother from brother,<br />you'll find that the trio resemble each other.<br />The first isn't there, though he'll come beyond doubt.<br />The second's departed, so he's not about.<br />The third and the smallest is right on the spot,<br />and manage without him the others could not.<br />Yet the third is a factor with which to be reckoned<br />because the first brother turns into the second.<br />You cannot stand back and observe number three,<br />for one of the others is all you will see.<br />So tell me, my child, are the three of them one?<br />Or are there but two? Or could there be none?<br />Just name them, and you will at once realize<br />that each rules a kingdom of infinite size.<br />They rule it together and are it as well.<br />In that, they're alike, so where do they dwell?</i><br /><br />The brothers described are the past, the present, and the future. Both the subject and theme of the novel is Time. Time is being surreptitiously stolen from the inhabitants of this indeterminate place by humorless men dressed in gray. As the general supply of time dwindles, the citizenry become more rushed and work harder for longer hours, slowly losing the capacity to enjoy any of the intangible pleasures of life let alone their material accumulations.<br /><br />The heroine is a child, Momo. When even her two trusty sidekicks, Guido and Beppo, succumb to the theft of time, all appears hopeless. The central image of this novel, which is rife with imagery, is the hour-lily, the source of time itself. They are cultivated by a Professor Hora. The tour we take of Professor Hora's headquarters and garden at the midpoint of this novel is a <i>tour de force</i> of imagination and imagery on the part of the author, <a href="http://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Ende" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael Ende</a>. A magical delight.<br /><br />My translation is by J. Maxwell Brownjohn. My usual word concerning translations. I spend nary a bit of time anymore worrying about whether my translation is a faithful one. If a translated novel works in English, I accept it without question and care not a whit whether it bears any relationship whatsoever to the original. This is a beautiful novel in English.<br /><br />In any event and in the end, it is incumbent upon little Momo under the instruction of Professor Horo to do battle alone against the men in gray, the thieves of time. The novel is paced well, and the denouement is exciting.<br /><br />Perhaps you should attempt to get around any preconceptions or biases concerning books of this sort and give it a try. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10330313270588549909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
