<div id="review_2168192256" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2168192256" />
    <a title="Khari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16880570-khari"><img alt="Khari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473471301p2/16880570.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2168192256?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khari" href="/user/show/16880570-khari">Khari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/27718.Momo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16880570-khari?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2168192256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9640603962941242116">I have finished. Finally. This book was interminable. <br/><br/>It was misnamed as well. Ende should have named his other book after the main character and called this one 'the never ending story' because that's what it was. Interminable.<br/><br/>Even as a bathroom book it was interminable. Reading even as much as a page at a time was agonizingly difficult. <br/><br/>It didn't help at all that the cover art was horrendous. Who in their right mind would draw a realistic picture of a ragged street waif complete with dirt as t</span>
  <span id="freeText9640603962941242116" style="display:none">I have finished. Finally. This book was interminable. <br /><br />It was misnamed as well. Ende should have named his other book after the main character and called this one 'the never ending story' because that's what it was. Interminable.<br /><br />Even as a bathroom book it was interminable. Reading even as much as a page at a time was agonizingly difficult. <br /><br />It didn't help at all that the cover art was horrendous. Who in their right mind would draw a realistic picture of a ragged street waif complete with dirt as the cover of a fantasy book moralizing about how we should all stop moving through time so quickly? I could understand such a waif on the front cover of say Oliver Twist, where that is the actual point of the story, but why focus on the girl's homeless status when that really doesn't matter at all to the story? Momo certainly doesn't view herself as the victim of society, or as a dispriviledged and under-represented minority. So why does the cover?<br /><br />I digress though, the cover doesn't particularly matter.<br /><br />The moral of the story, trite as it is, is good: take time to smell the roses. <br /><br />I am sure Ende would have been even more horrified if he had lived to see the advent of the internet and smart phones reducing our attention span to milliseconds, as he was quite horrified enough by the 70s to write this book encouraging people to enjoy their time. I think a lot of what he has to say is quite true, I simply couldn't abide the writing. This could be because it is a translated work, that is entirely possible. It was just so boring. I couldn't connect with anything or anyone. They all could have died in fire and ash and I would not have cared in the slightest. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9640603962941242116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BUyMxo/Gj0f46QLlNqPcwjhO0KR3/ocQxb5C6aZKEZU/auUUNJhGL1/CtoTBVtYd7hE3bLlzCXeewARYawnjDw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rmb/IKI21YpoHtUwwfr5BoHUv2MrhM5zg84ZEJj/d+WUQJbyGWgc4s81YVE2D/PZV4tYq+UJQBTYsF+hVbyFfw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10273890457533609082">Michael Andreas Helmuth Ende was a German writer of fantasy and children's literature. He was the son of the surrealist painter Edgar Ende.<br/><br/>Ende was one of the most popular and famous German authors of the 20th century, mostly due to the enormous success of his children's books. However, Ende was not strictly a children’s author, as he also wrote books for adults. Ende claimed, "It is for this chil</span>
  <span id="freeText10273890457533609082" style="display:none">Michael Andreas Helmuth Ende was a German writer of fantasy and children's literature. He was the son of the surrealist painter Edgar Ende.<br /><br />Ende was one of the most popular and famous German authors of the 20th century, mostly due to the enormous success of his children's books. However, Ende was not strictly a children’s author, as he also wrote books for adults. Ende claimed, "It is for this child in me, and in all of us, that I tell my stories," and that "[my books are] for any child between 80 and 8 years" (qtd. Senick 95, 97). Ende’s writing could be described as a surreal mixture of reality and fantasy. The reader is often invited to take a more interactive role in the story, and the worlds in his books often mirror our reality, using fantasy to bring light to the problems of an increasingly technological modern society.<br /><br />Ende was also known as a proponent of economic reform, and claimed to have had the concept of aging money in mind when writing <i>Momo</i>. He was interested in and influenced by anthroposophy.<br /><br /><i>Die unendliche Geschichte (The Neverending Story)</i> is Ende's best known work. Other books include <i>Momo</i> and <i>Jim Knopf und Lukas der Lokomotivführer (Jim Button and Luke the Engine Driver)</i>. Michael Ende's works have been translated into more than 40 languages and sold more than 20 million copies, and have been adapted into motion pictures, stage plays, operas and audio books.<br /><br />He died in Stuttgart of stomach cancer.<br /><br />AKA:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16296064.___________" title="Μίχαελ Έντε" rel="nofollow noopener">Μίχαελ Έντε</a> (Greek)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10273890457533609082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/517524-momo">Quotes from Momo</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;...it's like this. Sometimes, when you've a very long street ahead of you, you think how terribly long it is and feel sure you'll never get it swept. And then you start to hurry. You work faster and faster and every time you look up there seems to be just as much left to sweep as before, and you try even harder, and you panic, and in the end you're out of breath and have to stop--and still the street stretches away in front of you. That's not the way to do it.<br /><br />You must never think of the whole street at once, understand? You must only concentrate on the next step, the next breath, the next stroke of the broom, and the next, and the next. Nothing else.<br /><br />That way you enjoy your work, which is important, because then you make a good job of it. And that's how it ought to be.<br /><br />And all at once, before you know it, you find you've swept the whole street clean, bit by bit. what's more, you aren't out of breath. That's important, too...&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/17624-it-s-like-this-sometimes-when-you-ve-a-very-long-street">345 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;People never seemed to notice that, by saving time, they were losing something else. No one cared to admit that life was becoming ever poorer, bleaker and more monotonous. The ones who felt this most keenly were the children, because no one had time for them any more. But time is life itself, and life resides in the human heart. And the more people saved, the less they had.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/20099-people-never-seemed-to-notice-that-by-saving-time-they">245 likes</a>
